173:   ├──> Phase 1D (resolveSubaccount) — exercises subaccount-resolution
469:**Rule.** Every route with a `:subaccountId` URL parameter must call `resolveSubaccount(req.params.subaccountId, req.orgId!)` *before* using the subaccount ID downstream. `resolveSubaccount` (in `server/lib/subaccountResolution.ts`) verifies that the subaccount belongs to the requesting org and returns the canonical row; failing to call it allows a request scoped to org A to reference subaccount IDs belonging to org B (a horizontal-privilege-escalation primitive even with RLS in place, because a query that joins on subaccount-keyed rows would silently traverse).
475:| `server/routes/memoryReviewQueue.ts` | Has `:subaccountId` parameter; no `resolveSubaccount` call | Add `const subaccount = await resolveSubaccount(req.params.subaccountId, req.orgId!);` at the top of every handler that consumes `req.params.subaccountId`; pass `subaccount.id` (not the raw param) to service calls |
1433:| `server/routes/memoryReviewQueue.ts` | 1B + 1D (§4.2 + §4.4) | Remove direct `db` import; call new service. Add `resolveSubaccount(req.params.subaccountId, req.orgId!)` at every handler with the `:subaccountId` param. |
1438:| `server/routes/clarifications.ts` | 1B + 1D (§4.2 + §4.4) | Remove direct `db` import; extend existing `clarificationsService`. Add `resolveSubaccount(...)` at every handler with the `:subaccountId` param. |
1611:- [ ] **Subaccount-resolved.** Every route with a `:subaccountId` URL parameter calls `resolveSubaccount(req.params.subaccountId, req.orgId!)` before using the ID downstream.
1629:- **Prefer existing primitives over new abstractions.** This spec introduces zero new architectural primitives — every fix invokes `withOrgTx`, `withAdminConnection`, `withPrincipalContext`, `fromOrgId`, `llmRouter`, `canonicalDataService`, or `resolveSubaccount`. New primitives have a high evidentiary bar (per `prefer_existing_primitives_over_new_ones: yes`).

 succeeded in 1229ms:
server/lib\adminDbConnection.ts
server/lib\resolveSubaccount.ts

codex
- `§2.1` and `§4` contradict each other on Phase 1 sequencing: one says `0227` must be in `main` before Phase 1B starts, while the other says Phases 1A–1E ship together in one PR. Suggested fix: either split Phase 1 into at least two PRs (`0227` first, refactors second) or relax `§2.1` to require the migration be applied in-branch/CI before merge rather than already landed on `main`.

- `§4.1` and `§9.1` overstate the 0227 contract by assuming a single `DROP POLICY IF EXISTS <table>_org_isolation`, but the historical tables already use mixed names like `drop_zone_upload_audit_tenant_isolation`, `onboarding_bundle_configs_tenant_isolation`, and `trust_calibration_state_tenant_isolation`. Suggested fix: make 0227 enumerate and drop every historical policy name per table before creating the canonical policy.

- `§4.1` never gives the per-table historical policy-name inventory that makes the “replace any pre-existing policies” claim enforceable, which is exactly the failure mode `0213` avoided by listing `*_subaccount_isolation`, `*_read`, and `*_write` drops explicitly. Suggested fix: add a table under `§4.1` listing every historical policy name to drop for each affected table and mirror that list in the 0227 skeleton.

- `§4.5` says the `verify-rls-coverage` historical noise is “the same eight historical files,” but the proposed allowlist only names six files (`0204`–`0208`, `0212`) and silently omits `0202` and `0203`, even though `§3.5` and `0213` treat them as part of the repaired set. Suggested fix: either include `0202_reference_documents.sql` and `0203_reference_document_versions.sql` in the baseline rationale or explicitly state why they are excluded.

- `§3.5` says `verify-rls-coverage` found 19 violations “across 11 migrations,” but the migration list printed there contains 14 migrations. Suggested fix: correct either the migration count or the listed migrations so the captured gate state is internally consistent.

- `§0` still frames the scope as “all 47 findings, plus eight additional direct-DB-import violations and two additional coverage gaps,” which only reconciles to 57 and omits the `+8` historical-noise entries and `-2` dedupe later used to reach 63 in `§3.1`. Suggested fix: update every early “47 findings” framing line to explicitly reference the final `63 = 47 + 8 + 2 + 8 - 2` reconciliation.

- `§4.1`/`§9.1` claim the added `IS NOT NULL` guards make fail-closed semantics “unambiguous regardless of planner,” but the spec names no proof artifact, gate, or reproducer for that load-bearing statement. Suggested fix: either add a concrete SQL proof/reproducer reference or narrow the claim to “avoids NULL-dependent ambiguity” instead of asserting planner independence.

- `§4.1` says writes failing because `app.organisation_id` is unset is “the correct behaviour,” while `§15.1` says the invariant is defence-in-depth and “never rely on RLS alone.” Suggested fix: reword `§4.1` to call this a temporary fail-closed backstop and explicitly restate that Phase 1B must still add application-level org scoping on all write paths.

- `§4.4` reads as though only `memoryReviewQueue` and `clarifications` are relevant to the `:subaccountId` invariant, but several other Phase 1B routes (`subaccountAgents.ts`, `configDocuments.ts`, `automationConnectionMappings.ts`, `webLoginConnections.ts`) also carry `:subaccountId` and the spec never marks them “already compliant.” Suggested fix: add an explicit note/table distinguishing the two failing routes from the already-compliant Phase 1B routes.

- `§4.2`, `§4.4`, and `§12` have file/path drift against the repo: the real files are `server/lib/resolveSubaccount.ts`, `server/lib/adminDbConnection.ts`, `server/services/subaccountAgentService.ts`, `server/services/clarificationService.ts`, `server/services/conversationService.ts`, and `server/services/webLoginConnectionService.ts`. Suggested fix: normalize every target path and filename in the prose and inventory to the actual codebase names before implementation starts.

- `§5.4` gives an impossible fix for `server/routes/webhooks/ghlWebhook.ts` by telling the implementer to use `fromOrgId(req.orgId!, ...)`, but that route is unauthenticated and has no `req.orgId`. Suggested fix: change the guidance to construct principal context from `config.organisationId` and `dbAccount.subaccountId` after the webhook lookup.

- `§5.4` says `connectorPollingService.ts` has both `organisationId` and a known `subaccount_id` in scope, but most of that worker’s canonical upserts are org-scoped and only some later records expose `dbAccount.subaccountId`. Suggested fix: specify which calls use org-only `fromOrgId(organisationId)` and which can safely use `fromOrgId(organisationId, dbAccount.subaccountId)`.

- `§5.5` interprets `Literal action entries: 94, with readPath: 99` as “five actions missing `readPath`,” but that count direction does not support the diagnosis and could just as easily indicate duplicate or miscounted `readPath` fields. Suggested fix: replace the conclusion with “enumerate the offending slugs first,” then update the section with the actual five entries once identified.

- `§6.2.1` and `§12.1` violate the file-inventory rule by leaving `client/src/components/clientpulse/types.ts` versus `InterventionEditorTypes.ts` as an implementer choice instead of a single canonical file. Suggested fix: pick one filename now and use that single name everywhere in `§6` and `§12`.

- `§6.2.2`, `§12.1`, and `§12.2` use the wrong directory name (`client/src/components/skillAnalyzer/...`) while the repo path is `client/src/components/skill-analyzer/...`, and the inventory still leaves the step files as `<step components>`. Suggested fix: rename the path to `skill-analyzer` everywhere and enumerate `SkillAnalyzerImportStep.tsx`, `SkillAnalyzerExecuteStep.tsx`, `SkillAnalyzerProcessingStep.tsx`, and `SkillAnalyzerResultsStep.tsx` explicitly in `§12`.

- `§2.6`, `§3.2`, `§8.5`, and `§13.5` disagree on Phase 5 PR boundaries: one place says PRs are only per `§8.4` category, another says each of `§8.1`–`§8.4` is its own PR, and the DoD still bundles the whole phase. Suggested fix: define Phase 5 PR units once, then rewrite `§8.5` and `§13.5` to match those exact subsection-level boundaries.

- `§8.1`, `§8.4`, and `§12.1` hardcode `0228` and `0229` while also saying Phase 5 PRs can land “in any order,” so migration numbering breaks if the `toolCallsLog` PR lands first. Suggested fix: either require the `rate_limit_buckets` migration to land before any later Phase 5 migration or replace the hardcoded numbers with “next available migration number at implementation time.”

- `§8.1`, `§9.2`, and `§12` conflate `server/lib/testRunRateLimit.ts` with a public-form-only limiter, but that file is also used by `agents.ts`, `skills.ts`, `subaccountAgents.ts`, and `subaccountSkills.ts`. Suggested fix: state explicitly whether Phase 5 is rewriting the shared test-run/public limiter for all callers or splitting public-form rate limiting into a separate concretely named file and inventory entry.

- `§8.1`, `§12`, and `§13.5` make job registration load-bearing by requiring `rateLimitBucketCleanupJob.ts` to be scheduled, but they never name the concrete registration file that must change. Suggested fix: add the actual scheduler-registration file(s) to `§8.1` and `§12` (for example the queue/bootstrap module) so the work is implementable end to end.

- `§6.3`, `§8.4`, and `§13.5` escalate the server cycle target from `≤ 5` in Phase 3 to `0` in Phase 5, but `§8.4` only defines client-cycle follow-ons and never names a server-cycle cleanup item. Suggested fix: either add an explicit Phase 5 server-cycle tail item or keep the final DoD aligned with the Phase 3 `≤ 5` target plus deferred residual triage.

- `§2.4` forbids gate bypass via `# baseline-allow`, but `§5.7` and `§8.2` both prescribe inline `# baseline-allow` suppressions for warning gates, which is a direct process contradiction. Suggested fix: either carve warning-only gates out of the `§2.4` rule explicitly or replace those suppressions with a gate-owned baseline mechanism consistent with the Phase 1E approach.
